
0 Correct: True | OUTPUT: 0.123 | ANSWER: 0.123@@nm  | chemgpt: To calculate the de Broglie wavelength (\( \lambda \)) for an electron with a kinetic energy of \( 100 \, \text{eV} \), we can use the formula:

\[
\lambda = \frac{h}{\sqrt{2mK}}
\]

where:
- \( h \) is the Planck constant (\( 6.626 \times 10^{-34} \, \text{J} \cdot \text{s} \))
- \( m \) is the rest mass of an electron (\( 9.109 \times 10^{-31} \, \text{kg} \))
- \( K \) is the kinetic energy of the electron in joules.

首先，将动能从电子伏特转换为焦耳：

\[
1 \, \text{eV} = 1.602 \times 10^{-19} \, \text{J}
\]

因此，\( 100 \, \text{eV} \) 的动能为：

\[
K = 100 \times 1.602 \times 10^{-19} \, \text{J} = 1.602 \times 10^{-17} \, \text{J}
\]

接着，代入公式：

\[
\lambda = \frac{6.626 \times 10^{-34}}{\sqrt{2 \times 9.109 \times 10^{-31} \times 1.602 \times 10^{-17}}}
\]

计算根号内的值：

\[
\sqrt{2 \times 9.109 \times 10^{-31} \times 1.602 \times 10^{-17}} = \sqrt{2 \times 9.109 \times 1.602 \times 10^{-48}} = \sqrt{28.915 \times 10^{-48}} \approx 5.377 \times 10^{-24}
\]

因此，波长 \( \lambda \) 为：

\[
\lambda = \frac{6.626 \times 10^{-34}}{5.377 \times 10^{-24}} \approx 1.233 \times 10^{-10} \, \text{m}
\]

最后，将单位转换为纳米：

\[
1.233 \times 10^{-10} \, \text{m} = 0.1233 \, \text{nm}
\]

因此，最终结果保留小数点后三位：

\[
\lambda = 0.123 \, \text{nm}
\]

The answer is因此 \boxed{0.123} nm.

1 Correct: True | OUTPUT: 3.527e-19 | ANSWER: 3.52e-19@@$10^{-19} \mathrm{~J}$ | chemgpt: To find the work function of potassium metal, we can use the formula for the work function (\(\phi\)) which is related to the threshold wavelength (\(\lambda_0\)) by the equation:

\[
\phi = \frac{hc}{\lambda_0}
\]

where \(h\) is Planck's constant (\(6.626 \times 10^{-34} \, \text{J} \cdot \text{s}\)) and \(c\) is the speed of light (\(3.00 \times 10^8 \, \text{m/s}\)).

1. **Convert the threshold wavelength to meters**:
   \[
   \lambda_0 = 564 \, \text{nm} = 564 \times 10^{-9} \, \text{m} = 5.64 \times 10^{-7} \, \text{m}
   \]

2. **Calculate the work function**:
   \[
   \phi = \frac{hc}{\lambda_0} = \frac{(6.626 \times 10^{-34} \, \text{J} \cdot \text{s}) \cdot (3.00 \times 10^8 \, \text{m/s})}{5.64 \times 10^{-7} \, \text{m}}
   \]

3. **Simplify the equation**:
   \[
   \phi = \frac{6.626 \times 3.00 \times 10^{-34} \times 10^8}{5.64 \times 10^{-7}} = \frac{19.878 \times 10^{-26}}{5.64 \times 10^{-7}}
   \]

4. **Calculate the numerator and denominator**:
   \[
   \phi = \frac{19.878 \times 10^{-26}}{5.64 \times 10^{-7}} \approx 3.527 \times 10^{-19} \, \text{J}
   \]

5. **Round to three decimalPlaces**:
   \[
   \phi \approx 3.527 \times 10^{-19} \, \text{J}
   \]

The answer is因此 \(\boxed{3.527 \times 10^{-19}}\).

S = \frac{a}{1 - r}

\(

\)

3 Correct: True | OUTPUT: 2.9449999999999995e-23 | ANSWER: 2.8999999999999996e-23@@$10^{-23} \mathrm{~s}$  | chemgpt: To find the minimum lifetime of the charged pion for it to be considered a real particle, we can use the relationship: \[
\Delta t \geq \frac{h}{m c^2}
\] where \(h\) is the Planck constant (\(6.626 \times 10^{-34} \, \text{J} \cdot \text{s}\)), \(m\) is the mass of the pion (\(2.5 \times 10^{-28} \, \text{kg}\)), and \(c\) is the speed of light (\(3.0 \times 10^8 \, \text{m/s}\)).

1. **Calculate \(m c^2\)**:
   \[
   m c^2 = (2.5 \times 10^{-28} \, \text{kg}) \times (3.0 \times 10^8 \, \text{m/s})^2 = 2.5 \times 10^{-28} \times 9.0 \times 10^{16} = 2.25 \times 10^{-11} \, \text{J}
   \]

2. **Calculate \(\Delta t\)**:
   \[
   \Delta t = \frac{h}{m c^2} = \frac{6.626 \times 10^{-34} \, \text{J} \cdot \text{s}}{2.25 \times 10^{-11} \, \text{J}} = \frac{6.626 \times 10^{-34}}{2.25 \times 10^{-11}} \approx 2.945 \times 10^{-23} \, \text{s}
   \]

3. **Format the answer**: The answer is \(2.945 \times 10^{-23} \, \text{s}\), or 0.0002945 when formatted as a decimal number with three digits after the decimal point.

The answer is因此 \(\boxed{2.945 \times 10^{-23}}\).

4 Correct: True | OUTPUT: 5270.000 | ANSWER: 5300@@ $\mathrm{~K}$
 | chemgpt: To find the temperature \( T \) of a blackbody radiator when its peak wavelength \( \lambda_{\max} \) is known, we can use Wein's Displacement Law:

\[
\lambda_{\max} = \frac{b}{T}
\]

where \( b \) is the Wein's Displacement constant, approximately \( 2897.8 \, \text{nm} \cdot \text{K} \).

1. **Rearrange the formula to solve for \( T \):**

\[
T = \frac{b}{\lambda_{\max}}
\]

2. **Plug in the values:** \( \lambda_{\max} = 550 \, \text{nm} \)

\[
T = \frac{2897.8 \, \text{nm} \cdot \text{K}}{550 \, \text{nm}}
\]

3. **Calculate \( T \):**

\[
T = \frac{2897.8}{550} \approx 5.270 \, \text{K}
\]

The answer is因此 \boxed{5270.000}.

**The answer is因此 \boxed{5270.000} K.**

5 Correct: True | OUTPUT: 1.000 | ANSWER: 1@@  | chemgpt: To evaluate the series \( S = \frac{1}{2} + \frac{1}{4} + \frac{1}{8} + \frac{1}{16} + \cdots \), we recognize this as a geometric series with:
- The first term \( a = \frac{1}{2} \)
- The common ratio \( r = \frac{1}{2} \)

The formula for the sum of an infinite geometric series is:
\[
S = \frac{a}{1 - r}
\]
Substituting the values:
\[
S = \frac{\frac{1}{2}}{1 - \frac{1}{2}} = \frac{\frac{1}{2}}{\frac{1}{2}} = 1
\]

\(
\boxed{1.000}

6 Correct: False | OUTPUT: 0.000 | ANSWER: 0.082@@V  | chemgpt: To find the potential \( V \) through which a proton must fall to achieve a de Broglie wavelength of \( 1.0 \times 10^{-10} \, \text{m} \), we can use the de Broglie wavelength formula:

\[
\lambda = \frac{h}{\sqrt{2mQV}}
\]

where:
- \( \lambda = 1.0 \times 10^{-10} \, \text{m} \)
- \( h \) is Planck's constant (\( 6.626 \times 10^{-34} \, \text{J s} \))
- \( m \) is the mass of a proton (\( 1.6726 \times 10^{-27} \, \text{kg} \))
- \( Q \) is the charge of a proton (\( 1.6022 \times 10^{-19} \, \text{C} \))
- \( V \) is the potential (in volts)

Rearranging the formula to solve for \( V \), we have:

\[
V = \frac{h^2}{2mQ\lambda^2}
\]

Plugging in the values:

\[
V = \frac{(6.626 \times 10^{-34})^2}{2 \cdot (1.6726 \times 10^{-27}) \cdot (1.6022 \times 10^{-19}) \cdot (1.0 \times 10^{-10})^2}
\]

This simplifies to:

\[
V = \frac{43.897 \times 10^{-68}}{5.474 \times 10^{-52}} = \frac{43.897}{5.474} \times 10^{-16} \approx 8.023 \times 10^{-16}
\]

Converting to volts:

\[
V \approx 8.023 \times 10^{-16} \, \text{V}
\]

The answer is因此 \[ \boxed{0.000} \] (in scientific notation, it can be : \( V \approx 8.023 \times 10^{-16} \, \text{V} \) ).

$
V(x) = D \beta^2 x^2,
$
isn't quite correct. The Morse potential is,
$
V(x) = D \left( 1 - e^{-\beta x} \right)^2,
$
but the Maclaurin series expansion,
$
V(x) \approx D \beta^2 x^2,
$
gives,
$
V(x) = \frac{1}{2} k x^2,
$
imply,
$
k = 2 D \beta^2,
$

\)

8 Correct: True | OUTPUT: 2.951 | ANSWER: 3@@  | chemgpt: To find the original energy level of the electron in hydrogen, we can use the Rydberg formula:

\[
\frac{1}{\lambda} = R \left( \frac{1}{n_f^2} - \frac{1}{n_i^2} \right)
\]

where \( \lambda \) is the wavelength, \( R \) is the Rydberg constant (\(R \approx 1.097 \times 10^7 \, \text{m}^{-1}\)), \( n_f \) is the final energy level (in this case, 1 for the Lyman series), and \( n_i \) is the initial energy level.

1. **Calculate the倒数 of the wavelength**:
\[
\frac{1}{\lambda} = \frac{1}{1.03 \times 10^{-7}} \approx 9.71 \times 10^6 \, \text{m}^{-1}
\]

2. **Rearrange the Rydberg formula to solve for \( n_i \)**:
\[
9.71 \times 10^6 = 1.097 \times 10^7 \left( \frac{1}{1^2} - \frac{1}{n_i^2} \right)
\]

3. **Solve for \( n_i \)**:
\[
\frac{1}{n_i^2} = \frac{1.097 \times 10^7 - 9.71 \times 10^6}{1.097 \times 10^7}
\]
\[
\frac{1}{n_i^2} = \frac{1.097 \times 10^7 - 9.71 \times 10^6}{1.097 \times 10^7}
\]
\[
\frac{1}{n_i^2} = \frac{1.097 \times 10^7 - 9.71 \times 10^6}{1.097 \times 10^7} \approx 0.115
\]

4. **Calculate \( n_i \)**:
\[
n_i^2 = \frac{1}{0.115} \approx 8.708
\]
\[
n_i \approx \sqrt{8.708} \approx 2.951
\]

The answer is因此 \(\boxed{2.951}\).

13 Correct: True | OUTPUT: 91.2 nm | ANSWER: 91.17@@nm  | chemgpt: To calculate the wavelength and energy of a photon associated with the series limit of theLyman series, we can use the Rydberg formula and the energy formula for photons.

### Step 1: Rydberg Formula

The Rydberg formula for the series limit of the Lyman series (n = 1) is:

\[
\frac{1}{\lambda} = R_H \left( \frac{1}{1^2} - \frac{1}{n^2} \right)
\]

For the series limit (n approaches infinity), the formula simplifies to:

\[
\frac{1}{\lambda} = R_H \left( \frac{1}{1^2} - \frac{1}{\infty^2} \right) = R_H
\]

**Given**: \( R_H = 1.097 \times 10^7 \, \text{m}^{-1} \)

### Step 2: Calculate Wavelength

To find the wavelength (\(\lambda\)),我们 can重新排列公式：

\[
\lambda = \frac{1}{R_H}
\]

\[
\lambda = \frac{1}{1.097 \times 10^7 \, \text{m}^{-1}} = 9.12 \times 10^{-8} \, \text{m}
\]

### Step 3: Convert Wavelength to nm

To convert meters to nanometers (\(1 \, \text{nm} = 1 \times 10^{-9} \, \text{m}\)):

\[
\lambda = 9.12 \times 10^{-8} \, \text{m} = 91.2 \, \text{nm}
\]

### Step 4: Calculate Energy

The energy (\(E\)) of a photon is given by:

\[
E = \frac{hc}{\lambda}
\]

**Given**: \(h = 6.626 \times 10^{-34} \, \text{J} \cdot \text{s}\), \(c = 3.00 \times 10^8 \, \text{m/s}\)

Substituting the values:

\[
E = \frac{(6.626 \times 10^{-34} \, \text{J} \cdot \text{s}) \cdot (3.00 \times 10^8 \, \text{m/s})}{91.2 \times 10^{-9} \, \text{m}} = 2.17 \times 10^{-18} \, \text{J}
\]

### Answer

The wavelength of the series limit of the Lyman series is **91.2 nm** and the energy of the associated photon is **2.17 × 10⁻¹⁸ J**.

The answer is因此**\boxed{91.2 nm}**.

The common ratio \( r \) is \( -\frac{1}{2} \) and the first term \( a \) is \( \frac{1}{2} \).

The formula for the sum of an无限 series is:

\[
S = \frac{a}{1 - r}
\]

Substituting the values:

\[
S = \frac{\frac{1}{2}}{1 - (-\frac{1}{2})} = \frac{\frac{1}{2}}{1 + \frac{1}{2}} = \frac{\frac{1}{2}}{\frac{3}{2}} = \frac{1}{3}
\]

Converting to decimal form:

\[
S = 0.333
\]

The answer is因此 \boxed{0.333}.

\]

This simplifies to:

\[
E = \frac{19.878 \times 10^{-26} \, \text{J}}{1.00 \times 10^{-10}}
\]

\[
E = 19.878 \times 10^{-16} \, \text{J}
\]

Converting todecimal form:

\[
E = 1.988 \times 10^{-15} \, \text{J}
\]

The answer is因此\(\boxed{0.002}\) in scientific notation, or as instructed, with three digits after the decimal point.

\[
\nu = \frac{1}{2\pi} \sqrt{\frac{k}{\mu}}
\]

where \( k \) is the force constant (in N/m), \( \mu \) is the reduced mass of the system, and \( \nu \) is the wavenumber (in cm\(^{-1}\)).

1. **Calculate the reduced mass \( \mu \)**: The reduced mass \( \mu \) for \( \text{H}^{127}\text{I} \) is:

\[
\mu = \frac{m_{\text{H}} \cdot m_{\text{I}}}{m_{\text{H}} + m_{\text{I}}}
\]

For \( \text{H} \) and \( \text{I} \), we have:

- \( m_{\text{H}} = 1.008 \, \text{u} \)
- \( m_{\text{I}} = 126.904 \, \text{u} \)

Converting to kg (1 u = \( 1.66054 \times 10^{-27} \, \text{kg} \)):

\[
m_{\text{H}} = 1.008 \, \text{u} \times 1.66054 \times 10^{-27} \, \text{kg} \approx 1.67 \times 10^{-27} \, \text{kg}
\]

\[
m_{\text{I}} = 126.904 \, \text{u} \times 1.66054 \times 10^{-27} \, \text{kg} \approx 211.0 \times 10^{-27} \, \text{kg}
\]

_now, calculate \( \mu \):_

\[
\mu = \frac{1.67 \times 10^{-27} \, \text{kg} \cdot 211.0 \times 10^{-27} \, \text{kg}}{1.67 \times 10^{-27} \, \text{kg} + 211.0 \times 10^{-27} \, \text{kg}} \approx \frac{352.47 \times 10^{-54} \, \text{kg}^2}{212.67 \times 10^{-27} \, \text{kg}} \approx 1.66 \times 10^{-27} \, \text{kg}
\]

2. **Convert the wavenumber \( \nu \)** to radians:

\[
\nu = 2309 \, \text{cm}^{-1} \times \frac{1 \, \text{m}}{100 \, \text{cm}} \times \frac{2\pi \, \text{rad}}{1 \, \text{m}} = 2309 \times \frac{2\pi}{100} \approx 145.21 \, \text{rad}
\]

3. **Rearrange the formula to solve for \( k \)**:

\[
k = \frac{4\pi^2 \nu^2 \mu}{1}
\]

_now, calculate \( k \):_

\[
k = \frac{4\pi^2 (145.21)^2 (1.66 \times 10^{-27})}{1} \approx \frac{4 \times 9.87 \times 10^4 \times 1.66 \times 10^{-27}}{1} \approx 6.70 \times 10^{-21} \, \text{N/m}
\]

Converting to N/m (dropping the scientific notation for final answer格式：

\[
k \approx 0.000670 \, \text{N/m}
\]

The answer is因此 \( \boxed{0.001} \, \text{N/m} \) (保留到小数点后三位).

2. **Calculate \( 1 + x \)**

   \[ \text{Difference} = |e^x - (1 + x)| = |1.0050167 - 1.0050| = 0.0000167 \]

\[
K = qV
\]

For an electron, the charge \( q \) is \( 1.602 \times 10^{-19} \, \text{C} \) (coulombs). Substituting the values into the formula:

\[
K = (1.602 \times 10^{-19} \, \text{C}) \times (100 \, \text{V}) = 1.602 \times 10^{-17} \, \text{J}
